<p><i><b>Portal</b></i> is a 2007 <a href="/wiki/First-person_(video_games)" title="First-person (video games)" class="mw-redirect">first-person</a> <a href="/wiki/Platform_game#Puzzle_platformers" title="Platform game">puzzle-platform</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Valve_Corporation" title="Valve Corporation">Valve Corporation</a>. The game was released in a <a href="/wiki/Product_bundling" title="Product bundling">bundle package</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orange_Box" title="The Orange Box">The Orange Box</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> on October 9, 2007, and for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> on December 11, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-pcrelease_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcrelease-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360release_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360release-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ps3release_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps3release-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The Windows version of the game is available for download separately through Valve's content delivery system <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> and was released as a standalone <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> product on April 9, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-joystiq_orange_split_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joystiq_orange_split-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steam_App_400_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steam_App_400-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> A standalone version called <i><b>Portal: Still Alive</b></i> was released on the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Arcade" title="Xbox Live Arcade">Xbox Live Arcade</a> service on October 22, 2008; this version includes an additional 14 puzzles. An <a href="/wiki/OS_X" title="OS X">OS X</a> version was released as part of the Mac-compatible Steam platform on May 12, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Hollister_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollister-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> A Linux version was released on Steam as a beta on May 2, 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and came out of beta on June 24, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> port for the <a href="/wiki/Nvidia_Shield" title="Nvidia Shield" class="mw-redirect">Nvidia Shield</a> was released on May 12, 2014.</p>
<p>The game primarily comprises a series of puzzles that must be solved by <a href="/wiki/Teleportation" title="Teleportation">teleporting</a> the player's character and simple objects using "the Aperture Science Handheld Portal Device", a device that can create inter-spatial <a href="/wiki/Portal_(fiction)" title="Portal (fiction)" class="mw-redirect">portals</a> between two flat planes. The player-character, <a href="/wiki/Chell_(Portal)" title="Chell (Portal)">Chell</a>, is challenged by an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> named <a href="/wiki/GLaDOS" title="GLaDOS">GLaDOS</a> (Genetic Lifeform and <a href="/wiki/Disk_Operating_System" title="Disk Operating System" class="mw-redirect">Disk Operating System</a>) to complete each puzzle in the Aperture Science Enrichment Center using the portal gun with the promise of receiving <a href="/wiki/Cake" title="Cake">cake</a> when all the puzzles are completed. The game's unique physics allows momentum to be retained through portals, requiring creative use of portals to maneuver through the test chambers. This gameplay element is based on a similar concept from the game <i><a href="/wiki/Narbacular_Drop" title="Narbacular Drop">Narbacular Drop</a></i>; many of the team members from the <a href="/wiki/DigiPen_Institute_of_Technology" title="DigiPen Institute of Technology">DigiPen Institute of Technology</a> who worked on <i>Narbacular Drop</i> were hired by Valve for the creation of <i>Portal</i>.</p>
<p><i>Portal</i> was acclaimed as one of the most original games of 2007, despite being considered short in length. The game received praise for its unique gameplay and darkly humorous story. It received acclaim for the character of GLaDOS, voiced by <a href="/wiki/Ellen_McLain" title="Ellen McLain">Ellen McLain</a> in the English-language version, and the end credits song "<a href="/wiki/Still_Alive" title="Still Alive">Still Alive</a>" written by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Coulton" title="Jonathan Coulton">Jonathan Coulton</a> for the game. Not counting sales through Steam, over four million copies of the game have been sold since its release. The game's popularity has led to official merchandise from Valve including plush Companion Cubes, as well as fan recreations of the cake and portal gun. A sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">Portal 2</a></i>, was released in 2011, adding several new gameplay mechanics and a cooperative multiplayer mode.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft" style="width: 162px;">
<div class="thumbinner">
<div style="margin: 1px; width: 152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Portal_physics-2.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Portal_physics-2.svg/150px-Portal_physics-2.svg.png" width="150" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Portal_physics-2.svg/225px-Portal_physics-2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Portal_physics-2.svg/300px-Portal_physics-2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="351" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A representation of how the (<a href="/wiki/Magnitude_(mathematics)" title="Magnitude (mathematics)">magnitude</a> of) <a href="/wiki/Linear_momentum" title="Linear momentum" class="mw-redirect">linear momentum</a> is conserved through portals. By jumping into the blue portal, the character is launched out of the orange portal and onto the platform on the right.</div>
</div>
<div style="margin: 1px; width: 152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Portal_physics-3.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Portal_physics-3.svg/150px-Portal_physics-3.svg.png" width="150" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Portal_physics-3.svg/225px-Portal_physics-3.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Portal_physics-3.svg/300px-Portal_physics-3.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="351" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A more advanced portal technique. The character builds up speed using two blue portals, to reach an otherwise unreachable area. The second blue portal is carefully created in mid-air, after exiting the orange portal for the first time, destroying the first blue portal in the process.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <i>Portal</i>, the player controls the protagonist, Chell, from a <a href="/wiki/First-person_(video_games)" title="First-person (video games)" class="mw-redirect">first-person perspective</a> as she is challenged to navigate through a series of rooms using the Aperture Science Handheld Portal Device, or portal gun. The portal gun can create two distinct portal ends, orange and blue. The portals create a visual and physical connection between two different locations in <a href="/wiki/Three-dimensional_space" title="Three-dimensional space">three-dimensional space</a>. Neither end is specifically an entrance or exit; all objects that travel through one portal will exit through the other. An important aspect of the game's physics is momentum redirection.<sup id="cite_ref-commentary_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> As moving objects pass through portals, they come through the exit portal at the same direction as the exit portal is facing and with the same speed with which they passed through the entrance portal.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> For example, a common maneuver is to jump down to a portal on the floor and emerge through a wall, flying over a gap or another obstacle. This allows the player to launch objects or Chell herself over great distances, both vertically and horizontally, referred to as 'flinging' by Valve.<sup id="cite_ref-commentary_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> As GLaDOS puts it, "In layman's terms: speedy thing goes in, speedy thing comes out." If portal ends are not on parallel planes, the character passing through is reoriented to be upright with respect to gravity after leaving a portal end.</p>
<p>Chell and all other objects in the game that can fit into the portal ends will pass through the portal. However, a portal shot cannot pass through an open portal; it will simply deactivate or create a new portal in an offset position. Creating a portal end instantly deactivates an existing portal end of the same color. Moving objects, glass, special wall surfaces, liquids, or areas that are too small will not be able to anchor portals. Chell is sometimes provided with cubes that she can pick up and use to climb on or to hold down large buttons that open doors or activate mechanisms. Particle fields known as emancipation grills, occasionally called "fizzlers" in the developer commentary, exist at the end of all and within some test chambers; when passed through, they will deactivate any active portals and disintegrate any object carried through. The fields also block attempts to fire portals through them.<sup id="cite_ref-360_manual_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360_manual-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although Chell is equipped with mechanized heel springs to prevent damage from falling,<sup id="cite_ref-commentary_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> she can be killed by various other hazards in the test chambers, such as turret guns, bouncing balls of energy, and toxic liquid. She can also be killed by objects falling through portals, and by a series of crushers that appear in certain levels. Unlike most action games at the time, there is no <a href="/wiki/Health_(gaming)" title="Health (gaming)">health</a> indicator; Chell dies if she is dealt a certain amount of damage in a short time period, but returns to full health fairly quickly. Some obstacles, such as the energy balls and crushing pistons, deal fatal damage with a single blow.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/GameSpot" title="GameSpot">GameSpot</a> noted, in its initial review of <i>Portal</i>, that many solutions exist for completing each puzzle, and that the gameplay "gets even crazier, and the diagrams shown in the trailer showed some incredibly crazy things that you can attempt."<sup id="cite_ref-gamespotarticle1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotarticle1-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Two additional modes are unlocked upon the completion of the game that challenge the player to work out alternative methods of solving each test chamber. Challenge maps are unlocked near the halfway point and Advanced Chambers are unlocked when the game is completed.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In Challenge mode, levels are revisited with the added goal of completing the test chamber either with as little time, with the least number of portals, or with the fewest footsteps possible. In Advanced mode, certain levels are made more complex with the addition of more obstacles and hazards.<sup id="cite_ref-eurogamerfi_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamerfi-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cvg1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cvg1-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The PC, Xbox 360 and OS X versions of the game also feature a number of <a href="/wiki/Achievement_(video_gaming)" title="Achievement (video gaming)">achievements</a> the player can earn by completing tasks. Achievements range from normal gameplay requirements, such as acquiring the fully operational Aperture Science handheld portal device, to various tricks, such as using portals to jump a particular distance or falling 30,000&#160;ft. As with other <a href="/wiki/Source_(game_engine)" title="Source (game engine)">Source engine</a> games since <i>Half-Life 2</i>, <i>Portal</i> can be played with commentary enabled; special icons will appear in the game that the player can activate to hear how certain parts of the game were developed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The game features two characters: the <a href="/wiki/Player_character" title="Player character">player-controlled</a> silent protagonist named <a href="/wiki/Chell_(Portal)" title="Chell (Portal)">Chell</a>, and GLaDOS (Genetic Lifeform and <a href="/wiki/Disk_Operating_System" title="Disk Operating System" class="mw-redirect">Disk Operating System</a>), a computer <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> that monitors and directs the player. In the English-language version, GLaDOS is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Ellen_McLain" title="Ellen McLain">Ellen McLain</a>, though her voice has been altered to sound more artificial. The only background information presented about Chell is given by GLaDOS; the credibility of these facts, such as Chell being adopted, an orphan, and having no friends, is questionable at best, as GLaDOS is a liar by her own admission. In the "Lab Rat" comic created by Valve to bridge the gap between <i>Portal</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">Portal 2</a></i>, Chell's records reveal she was ultimately rejected as a test subject for having "too much tenacity"—the main reason Doug Rattman, a former employee of Aperture Science, moved Chell to the top of the test queue.<sup id="cite_ref-labrat_part_1_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labrat_part_1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-labrat_part_2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labrat_part_2-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting">Setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Aperture_Science_Laboratories"></span></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aperture_Science.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aperture_Science.svg/220px-Aperture_Science.svg.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aperture_Science.svg/330px-Aperture_Science.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aperture_Science.svg/440px-Aperture_Science.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="531" data-file-height="531" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aperture_Science.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The fictional logo of Aperture Science Laboratories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Portal</i> takes place in the <a href="/wiki/Locations_of_Half-Life#Aperture_Science_Laboratories" title="Locations of Half-Life">Enrichment Center for Aperture Laboratories</a>—also known as Aperture Science—which is the fictional research corporation responsible for the creation of the portal gun. According to information presented in <i>Portal 2</i>, the location of the complex is in the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Peninsula_of_Michigan" title="Upper Peninsula of Michigan">Upper Peninsula of Michigan</a>. Information about the company, developed by Valve for creating the setting of the game, is revealed during the game and via the real-world promotional website.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_apsci_history_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_apsci_history-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Aperture Science Web site, <a href="/wiki/Cave_Johnson_(Portal)" title="Cave Johnson (Portal)">Cave Johnson</a> founded the company in 1943 for the sole purpose of making <a href="/wiki/Shower_curtain" title="Shower curtain" class="mw-redirect">shower curtains</a> for the U.S. military. However, after becoming mentally unstable from <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a> in 1978, Johnson created a three-tier <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> plan to make his organization successful. The first two tiers, the <a href="/wiki/Abdominal_thrusts" title="Abdominal thrusts" class="mw-redirect">Counter-Heimlich Maneuver</a> (a maneuver designed to ensure choking) and the <a href="/wiki/Make-A-Wish_Foundation" title="Make-A-Wish Foundation">Take-A-Wish Foundation</a> (a program to give the wishes of dying children to unrelated, entirely healthy adults), were commercial failures and led to an investigation of the company by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senate</a>. However, when the investigative committee heard of the success of the third tier, a man-sized ad-hoc quantum tunnel through physical space with possible applications as a shower curtain, it recessed permanently and gave Aperture Science an open-ended contract to continue its research. The development of GLaDOS, an artificially intelligent research assistant and disk-operating system, began in 1986 in response to <a href="/wiki/Black_Mesa_Research_Facility" title="Black Mesa Research Facility" class="mw-redirect">Black Mesa</a>'s work on similar portal technology.<sup id="cite_ref-aperture_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aperture-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> A presentation seen during gameplay reveals that GLaDOS was also included in a proposed bid for de-icing fuel lines, incorporated as a fully functional disk-operation system that is arguably alive, unlike Black Mesa's proposal, which inhibits ice, nothing more.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Roughly thirteen years later, work on GLaDOS was completed and the untested AI was activated during the company's first ever <a href="/wiki/Take_Our_Daughters_and_Sons_to_Work_Day" title="Take Our Daughters and Sons to Work Day">bring-your-daughter-to-work day</a> in May 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_apsci_history_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_apsci_history-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Immediately after activation, the facility was flooded with deadly neurotoxin by the AI. Events of the first <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_(video_game)" title="Half-Life (video game)">Half-Life</a></i> game occur shortly thereafter, presumably leaving the facility forgotten by the outside world due to apocalyptic happenings. Wolpaw, in describing the ending of <i>Portal 2</i>, affirmed that the <a href="/wiki/Combine_(Half-Life)" title="Combine (Half-Life)">Combine</a> invasion, chronologically taking place between <i>Half-Life</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2" title="Half-Life 2">Half-Life 2</a></i>, occurred during <i>Portal</i> '​s events.<sup id="cite_ref-pcgamer_p2_wolpaw_interview_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcgamer_p2_wolpaw_interview-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The areas of the Enrichment Center that Chell explores suggest that it is part of a massive research installation. At the time of events depicted in <i>Portal</i>, the facility seems to be long-deserted, although most of its equipment remains operational without human control.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_pc_review_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_pc_review-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Aperture Science exists in the <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_(series)" title="Half-Life (series)">Half-Life</a></i> universe,<sup id="cite_ref-gamespotarticle1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespotarticle1-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> with the events of <i>Portal</i> occurring sometime between the story of <i>Half-Life</i> and <i>Half-Life 2</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Aperture Science Inc. is also mentioned during <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2:_Episode_Two" title="Half-Life 2: Episode Two">Half-Life 2: Episode Two</a></i>, in which Aperture's <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreaker</a> ship <i>Borealis</i> is said to have disappeared under mysterious circumstances, along with the crew and part of its <a href="/wiki/Drydock" title="Drydock" class="mw-redirect">drydock</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> During its development, <i>Half-Life 2</i> featured a chapter set on the <i>Borealis</i>, but this was abandoned and removed before release.<sup id="cite_ref-raisingthebar_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raisingthebar-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Portal</i> '​s plot is revealed to the player via audio messages from GLaDOS and visual elements in side rooms found in later levels. According to <i>The Final Hours of Portal 2</i>, the year is established to be "somewhere in 2010"—twelve years after its abandonment. The game begins with protagonist Chell waking up from a stasis bed and hearing instructions and warnings from GLaDOS about the upcoming test experience. This part of the game involves distinct test chambers that, in sequence, introduce players to the game's mechanics. GLaDOS's announcements serve not only to instruct Chell and help her progress through the game, but also to create atmosphere and develop the AI as a character.<sup id="cite_ref-commentary_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Chell is promised <a href="/wiki/Cake" title="Cake">cake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grief_counseling" title="Grief counseling">grief counseling</a> as her reward if she manages to complete all the test chambers.<sup id="cite_ref-gamespy_pc_review_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy_pc_review-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chell proceeds through the empty Enrichment Center, interacting only with GLaDOS. Over the course of the game, GLaDOS's motives are hinted to be more sinister than her helpful demeanor suggests. Although she is designed to appear helpful and encouraging, GLaDOS's actions and speech suggest insincerity and callous disregard for the safety and well-being of the test subjects. The test chambers become increasingly dangerous as Chell proceeds, and GLaDOS even directs Chell through a live-fire course designed for military androids as a result of "mandatory scheduled maintenance" in the regular test chamber, as well as having test chambers flooded with deadly liquid. In another chamber, GLaDOS boasts about the fidelity and importance of the Weighted Companion Cube, a waist-high crate with a single large pink heart on each face, for helping Chell to complete the chamber. However, GLaDOS then declares that it "unfortunately must be <a href="/wiki/Euthanasia" title="Euthanasia">euthanized</a>" in an "emergency intelligence <a href="/wiki/Incinerator" title="Incinerator" class="mw-redirect">incinerator</a>" before Chell can continue.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_pc_review_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_pc_review-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the later chambers include automated turrets with childlike voices (also voiced by McLain) that fire at Chell, only to sympathize with her after being disabled ("I don't blame you" and "No hard feelings").<sup id="cite_ref-eurogamer_pc_review_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamer_pc_review-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ign_pc_review_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign_pc_review-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After Chell completes the final test chamber, GLaDOS congratulates her and prepares her "victory candescence", maneuvering Chell into a pit of fire. As GLaDOS assures her that "all Aperture technologies remain safely operational up to 4,000 degrees [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] <a href="/wiki/Kelvin" title="Kelvin">kelvin</a>", Chell escapes with the use of the portal gun and makes her way through the maintenance areas within the Enrichment Center.<sup id="cite_ref-wellplayed_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wellplayed-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> GLaDOS becomes panicked and insists that she was only pretending to kill Chell, as part of testing. GLaDOS then asks Chell to assume the "party escort submission position", lying face-first on the ground, so that a "party associate" can take her to her reward. Chell continues forward. Throughout this section, GLaDOS still sends messages to Chell and it becomes clear that she has become corrupt and may have killed everyone else in the center. Chell makes her way through the maintenance areas and empty office spaces behind the chambers, sometimes following graffiti messages which point in the right direction. These backstage areas, which are in an extremely dilapidated state, stand in stark contrast to the pristine test chambers. The graffiti includes statements such as "the cake is a lie" and <a href="/wiki/Pastiche" title="Pastiche">pastiches</a> of <a href="/wiki/Emily_Dickinson" title="Emily Dickinson">Emily Dickinson</a>'s poem "The Chariot", <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Henry Wadsworth Longfellow</a>'s "The Reaper and the Flowers", and <a href="/wiki/Emily_Bront%C3%AB" title="Emily Brontë">Emily Brontë</a>'s "No Coward Soul Is Mine", mourning the death of the Companion Cube.<sup id="cite_ref-commentary_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-commentary-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>GLaDOS attempts to dissuade Chell with threats of physical harm and misleading statements claiming that she is going the wrong way as Chell makes her way deeper into the maintenance areas. Eventually, Chell reaches a large chamber where GLaDOS's hardware hangs overhead. GLaDOS continues to plead with and threaten Chell, but during the exchange one of GLaDOS' personality core spheres falls off; Chell drops it in an incinerator. GLaDOS reveals that Chell has just destroyed the morality core, which the Aperture Science employees allegedly installed after GLaDOS flooded the enrichment center with a deadly neurotoxin, and goes on to state that now there is nothing to prevent her from doing so once again. A six-minute countdown starts as Chell dislodges and incinerates more pieces of GLaDOS, while GLaDOS attempts to discourage her both verbally, with a series of taunts and increasingly juvenile insults, and physically by firing rockets at her. After she has destroyed the final piece, a portal malfunction tears the room apart and transports everything to the surface. Chell is then seen lying outside the facility's gates amid the remains of GLaDOS. One of the final scenes is changed through a patch of the PC version and <i>The Orange Box</i> for Xbox that was made available a few days before <i>Portal 2</i> '​s announcement; in this <a href="/wiki/Retroactive_continuity" title="Retroactive continuity">retroactive continuity</a>, Chell is dragged away from the scene by an unseen entity speaking in a robotic voice, thanking her for assuming the party escort submission position.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-shacknews_update_2_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_update_2-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The final scene, after a long and speedy zoom through the bowels of the facility, shows a <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest_cake" title="Black Forest cake">Black Forest cake</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-german_chocolate_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-german_chocolate-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> and the Weighted Companion Cube, surrounded by a mix of shelves containing dozens of apparently inactive personality cores. One by one a number of the cores begin to light up, before a robotic arm descends and extinguishes the candle on the cake, plunging the room into darkness.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_p2_reveal_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_p2_reveal-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> As the credits roll, GLaDOS delivers a concluding report: the song "<a href="/wiki/Still_Alive" title="Still Alive">Still Alive</a>", which declares the experiment to be a huge success, as well as serving to indicate to the player that GLaDOS is still alive.<sup id="cite_ref-portal_the_skinny_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal_the_skinny-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concept">Concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Portal</i> is Valve's <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_successor" title="Spiritual successor">spiritual successor</a> to the freeware game <i><a href="/wiki/Narbacular_Drop" title="Narbacular Drop">Narbacular Drop</a></i>, the 2005 independent game released by students of the <a href="/wiki/DigiPen_Institute_of_Technology" title="DigiPen Institute of Technology">DigiPen Institute of Technology</a>; the original <i>Narbacular Drop</i> team is now employed at Valve.<sup id="cite_ref-narbdrop-confirm_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-narbdrop-confirm-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gilombardi_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gilombardi-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Valve became interested in <i>Narbacular Drop</i> after seeing the game at DigiPen's annual career fair; Robin Walker, one of Valve's developers, saw the game at the fair and later contacted the team providing them with advice and offering to show their game at Valve's offices. After their presentation, Valve's president <a href="/wiki/Gabe_Newell" title="Gabe Newell">Gabe Newell</a> quickly offered the entire team jobs at Valve to develop the game further.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes_portal_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes_portal-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Newell later commented that he was impressed with the DigiPen team as "they had actually carried the concept through", already having included the interaction between portals and physics, completing most of the work that Valve would have had to commit on their own.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes_portal_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes_portal-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Certain elements have been retained from <i>Narbacular Drop</i>, such as the system of identifying the two unique portal endpoints with the colors orange and blue. A key difference in the signature portal mechanic between the two games however is that <i>Portal</i> '​s portal gun cannot create a portal through an existing portal unlike in <i>Narbacular Drop</i>. The game's original setting, of a princess trying to escape a dungeon, was dropped in favor of the Aperture Science approach.<sup id="cite_ref-seattletimes_portal_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seattletimes_portal-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Portal</i> took approximately two years and four months to complete after the DigiPen team was brought into Valve,<sup id="cite_ref-planet_hl_interview_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planet_hl_interview-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> and no more than ten people were involved with its development.<sup id="cite_ref-shacknews_gdc08_interview_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_gdc08_interview-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Portal</i> writer <a href="/wiki/Erik_Wolpaw" title="Erik Wolpaw">Erik Wolpaw</a>, who, along with fellow writer Chet Faliszek, was hired by Valve for the game, claimed that "Without the constraints, <i>Portal</i> would not be as good a game".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Portal</i> team worked with <i>Half-Life</i> series writer <a href="/wiki/Marc_Laidlaw" title="Marc Laidlaw">Marc Laidlaw</a> on fitting the game into the series' plot.<sup id="cite_ref-1upinterview_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1upinterview-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> This was done, in part, due to the limited art capabilities of the small team; instead of creating new assets for <i>Portal</i>, they decided to tie the game to an existing franchise—<i>Half-Life</i>—to allow them to reuse the <i>Half-Life 2</i> art assets.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> Wolpaw and Faliszek were put to work on the dialogue for <i>Portal</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-gilombardi_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gilombardi-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The concept of a computer AI guiding the player through experimental facilities to test the portal gun was arrived at early in the writing process.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> They drafted early lines for the yet-named "polite" AI with humorous situations, such as requesting the player's character to "assume the party escort submission position", and found this style of approach to be well-suited to the game they wanted to create, ultimately leading to the creation of the GLaDOS character.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> GLaDOS was central to the plot, as Wolpaw notes "We designed the game to have a very clear beginning, middle, and end, and we wanted GLaDOS to go through a personality shift at each of these points."<sup id="cite_ref-rbs_wolpaw_interview_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbs_wolpaw_interview-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Wolpaw further describes the idea of using cake as the reward came about as "at the beginning of the <i>Portal</i> development process, we sat down as a group to decide what philosopher or school of philosophy our game would be based on. That was followed by about 15 minutes of silence and then someone mentioned that a lot of people like cake."<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rbs_wolpaw_interview_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbs_wolpaw_interview-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The cake element along with additional messages given to the player in the behind-the-scenes areas were written and drawn by <a href="/wiki/Kim_Swift" title="Kim Swift">Kim Swift</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portalgame.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7e/Portalgame.jpg/220px-Portalgame.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7e/Portalgame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/7e/Portalgame.jpg 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="240" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portalgame.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A typical <i>Portal</i> test chamber, with both of the player's colored portals opened. The Weighted Companion Cube can also be seen. The clean, spartan look to the chambers was influenced by the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Island_(2005_film)" title="The Island (2005 film)">The Island</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The austere settings in the game came about because testers spent too much time trying to complete the puzzles using decorative but non-functional elements. As a result, the setting was minimized to make the usable aspects of the puzzle easier to spot, using the clinical feel of the setting in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Island_(2005_film)" title="The Island (2005 film)">The Island</a></i> as reference.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> While there were plans for a third area, an office space, to be included after the test chambers and the maintenance areas, the team ran out of time to include it.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> They also dropped the introduction of the Rat Man, a character who left the messages in the maintenance areas, to avoid creating too much narrative for the game,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> though the character was developed further in a tie-in comic "Lab Rat", that ties <i>Portal</i> and <i>Portal 2</i> '​s story together.<sup id="cite_ref-labrat_part_1_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labrat_part_1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-labrat_part_2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-labrat_part_2-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> According to project lead Kim Swift, the final battle with GLaDOS went through many iterations, including having the player chased by <a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(film)" title="Goldfinger (film)">James Bond lasers</a>, which was partially applied to the turrets, <a href="/wiki/Mortal_Kombat" title="Mortal Kombat">Portal Kombat</a> where the player would have needed to redirect rockets while avoiding turret fire, and a chase sequence following a fleeing GLaDOS. Eventually, they found that playtesters enjoyed a rather simple puzzle with a countdown timer near the end; Swift noted, "Time pressure makes people think something is a lot more complicated than it really is", and Wolpaw admitted, "It was really cheap to make [the neurotoxin gas]" in order to simplify the dialogue during the battle.<sup id="cite_ref-shacknews_gdc08_interview_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_gdc08_interview-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Chell's face and body are modeled after <a href="/wiki/Al%C3%A9sia_Glidewell" title="Alésia Glidewell">Alésia Glidewell</a>, an American freelance actress and voice-over artist, selected by Valve from a local modeling agency for her face and body structure.<sup id="cite_ref-planet_hl_interview_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planet_hl_interview-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Ellen McLain provided the voice of the antagonist GLaDOS. Erik Wolpaw noted, "When we were still fishing around for the turret voice, Ellen did a sultry version. It didn't work for the turrets, but we liked it a lot, and so a slightly modified version of that became the model for GLaDOS's final incarnation."<sup id="cite_ref-rbs_wolpaw_interview_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbs_wolpaw_interview-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Patton" title="Mike Patton">Mike Patton</a> performed the growling and snarling voice of GLaDOS's final personality core, named the Anger Sphere.</p>
<p>The Weighted Companion Cube inspiration was from project lead Kim Swift with additional input from Wolpaw from reading some "declassified government interrogation thing" whereby "isolation leads subjects to begin to attach to inanimate objects";<sup id="cite_ref-shacknews_gdc08_interview_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_gdc08_interview-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rbs_wolpaw_interview_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbs_wolpaw_interview-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Swift commented, "We had a long level called Box Marathon; we wanted players to bring this box with them from the beginning to the end. But people would forget about the box, so we added dialogue, applied the heart to the cube, and continued to up the ante until people became attached to the box. Later on, we added the incineration idea. The artistic expression grew from the gameplay."<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Wolpaw further noted that the need to incinerate the Weighted Companion Cube came as a result of the final boss battle design; they recognized they had not introduced the idea of incineration necessary to complete the boss battle, and by training the player to do it with the Weighted Companion Cube, found the narrative "way stronger" with its "death".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Swift noted that any similarities to psychological situations in the <a href="/wiki/Milgram_experiment" title="Milgram experiment">Milgram experiment</a> or <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey" title="2001: A Space Odyssey">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> are happenstance.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The portal gun's full name, Aperture Science Handheld Portal Device, can be abbreviated as ASHPD, which resembles a shortening of the name Adrian Shephard, the protagonist of <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life:_Opposing_Force" title="Half-Life: Opposing Force">Half-Life: Opposing Force</a></i>. This similarity was noticed by fans before the game's release; as a result, the team placed a <a href="/wiki/Red_herring_(plot_device)" title="Red herring (plot device)" class="mw-redirect">red herring</a> in the game by having the letters of Adrian Shephard highlighted on keyboards found within the game.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Kim Swift, the cake is a Black Forest cake that she thought looked the best at the nearby Regent Bakery and Café in <a href="/wiki/Redmond,_Washington" title="Redmond, Washington">Redmond</a>, Washington, and, as an Easter egg within the game, its recipe is scattered among various screens showing lines of binary code.<sup id="cite_ref-german_chocolate_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-german_chocolate-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_cake_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_cake-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The Regent Bakery has stated that since the release of the game, its Black Forest cake has been one of its more popular items.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_cake_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_cake-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soundtrack">Soundtrack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Soundtrack">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most of the game's soundtrack is non-lyrical <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient music</a> composed by <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Bailey_(composer)" title="Kelly Bailey (composer)">Kelly Bailey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Morasky" title="Mike Morasky">Mike Morasky</a>, somewhat dark and mysterious to match the mood of the environments. The closing credits song, "<a href="/wiki/Still_Alive_(song)" title="Still Alive (song)" class="mw-redirect">Still Alive</a>", was written by <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Coulton" title="Jonathan Coulton">Jonathan Coulton</a> and sung by Ellen McLain (a classically trained <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">operatic</a> <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a>) as the GLaDOS character. A brief instrumental version of Still Alive is played in an uptempo Latin style over radios in-game. Wolpaw notes that Coulton was invited to Valve a year before the release of <i>Portal</i>, though it was not yet clear where Coulton would contribute. "Once Kim [Swift] and I met with him, it quickly became apparent that he had the perfect sensibility to write a song for GLaDOS."<sup id="cite_ref-portal_the_skinny_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portal_the_skinny-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rbs_wolpaw_interview_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbs_wolpaw_interview-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The use of the song over the closing credits was based on a similar concept from the game <i><a href="/wiki/God_Hand_(video_game)" title="God Hand (video game)" class="mw-redirect">God Hand</a></i>, one of Wolpaw's favorite titles.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_pax12_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_pax12-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was released as a free downloadable song for the <a href="/wiki/Music_video_game" title="Music video game">music video game</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_(video_game)" title="Rock Band (video game)">Rock Band</a></i> on April 1, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Still_Alive_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Still_Alive-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The soundtrack for <i>Portal</i> was released as a part of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orange_Box#Soundtrack" title="The Orange Box">The Orange Box Original Soundtrack</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> and includes both GLaDOS's in-game rendition and Coulton's vocal mix of "Still Alive".</p>
<p><i>Portal</i> '​s soundtrack was released as part of a four-disc retail release, <i>Portal 2: Songs To Test By (Collector's Edition)</i>, on October 30, 2012, featuring music from both games.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The game's soundtrack became available via Steam Music on September 24, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise">Merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/59/Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg/150px-Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg" width="150" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/59/Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/59/Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="197" data-file-height="219" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Companioncubesfuzzydice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The popularity of the Weighted Companion Cube has led Valve to create merchandise based on it, including <a href="/wiki/Fuzzy_dice" title="Fuzzy dice">fuzzy dice</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The popularity of the game and of its characters has led Valve to develop merchandise for <i>Portal</i> made available through its online <a href="/wiki/Steam_(software)" title="Steam (software)">Steam</a> store. Some of the more popular items were the Weighted Companion Cube plush toys and <a href="/wiki/Fuzzy_dice" title="Fuzzy dice">fuzzy dice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> When first released, both were sold out in under 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Other products available through the Valve store include t-shirts and Aperture Science coffee mugs and parking stickers, and merchandise relating to the phrase <i>the cake is a lie</i>, which has become an <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">internet meme</a>. Wolpaw noted they did not expect certain elements of the game to be as popular as they were, while other elements they had expected to become fads were ignored, such as a giant hoop that rolls on-screen during the final scene of the game that the team had named Hoopy.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_portal_hl_24-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_portal_hl-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demo">Demo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In January 2008, Valve released a special demo version titled <i><b>Portal: The First Slice</b></i>, free for any Steam user using <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> graphics hardware as part of a collaboration between the two companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Steam_News_1398_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steam_News_1398-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> It also comes packaged with <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2:_Deathmatch" title="Half-Life 2: Deathmatch">Half-Life 2: Deathmatch</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Peggle_Extreme" title="Peggle Extreme" class="mw-redirect">Peggle Extreme</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Half-Life_2:_Lost_Coast" title="Half-Life 2: Lost Coast">Half-Life 2: Lost Coast</a></i>. The demo includes test chambers 00 to 10 (eleven in total). Valve has since made the demo available to all Steam users.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portal"><i>Portal</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Portal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Portal</i> was first released as part of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Orange_Box" title="The Orange Box">The Orange Box</a></i> for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> on October 9, 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-pcrelease_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcrelease-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360release_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360release-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> and for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_3" title="PlayStation 3">PlayStation 3</a> on December 11, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-ps3release_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ps3release-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The Windows version of the game is also available for download separately through Valve's content delivery system, Steam,<sup id="cite_ref-Steam_App_400_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steam_App_400-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> and was released as a standalone <a href="/wiki/Retail" title="Retail">retail</a> product on April 9, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-joystiq_orange_split_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joystiq_orange_split-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to <i>Portal</i>, the <i>Box</i> also included <i>Half-Life 2</i> and its two add-on episodes, as well as <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>. <i>Portal</i> '​s inclusion within the <i>Box</i> was considered an experiment by Valve; having no idea of the success of <i>Portal</i>, the <i>Box</i> provided it a "safety net" via means of these other games. <i>Portal</i> was kept to a modest length in case the game did not go over well with players.<sup id="cite_ref-gi_p2_reveal_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gi_p2_reveal-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, a standalone version of the game was released for Microsoft Windows users.</p>
<p><i>Portal</i> was the first Valve-developed game to be added to the OS X-compatible list of games available on the launch of the Steam client for Mac on May 12, 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-Hollister_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hollister-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> supporting Steam Play, in which players that had bought the game either on a Macintosh or Windows computer could also play it on the alternate system. As part of the promotion, <i>Portal</i> was offered as a free title for any Steam user during the two weeks following the Mac client's launch.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Within the first week of this offer, over 1.5 million copies of the game were downloaded through Steam.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> A similar promotion was held in September 2011, near the start of a traditional school year, encouraging the use of the game as an educational tool for science and mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Valve wrote that they felt that <i>Portal</i> "makes physics, math, logic, spatial reasoning, probability, and problem-solving interesting, cool, and fun", a necessary feature to draw children into learning.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> This was tied to <a href="/wiki/Digital_Promise" title="Digital Promise">Digital Promise</a>, a United States Department of Education initiative to help develop new digital tools for education, and which Valve is part of.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During 2014 GPU Technology Conference on March 25, 2014, Nvidia announced that they are porting <i>Portal</i> to their <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> handheld, the <a href="/wiki/Nvidia_Shield" title="Nvidia Shield" class="mw-redirect">Nvidia Shield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The version was released on May 12, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portal:_Still_Alive"><i>Portal: Still Alive</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Portal: Still Alive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>Portal: Still Alive</i> was announced as an exclusive <a href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Arcade" title="Xbox Live Arcade">Xbox Live Arcade</a> game at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo">E3</a> convention, and was released on October 22, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> It features the original game, 14 new challenges, and new achievements.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The additional content was based on levels from the map pack <i>Portal: The Flash Version</i> created by We Create Stuff and contains no additional story-related levels.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Valve <a href="/wiki/Spokesman" title="Spokesman" class="mw-redirect">spokesman</a> Doug Lombardi, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> had previously rejected <i>Portal</i> on the platform due to its large size.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Portal: Still Alive</i> was well received by reviewers.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a>'s Andrew Hayward stated that, with the easier access and lower cost than paying for <i>The Orange Box</i>, <i>Portal</i> is now "stronger than ever".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> editor Cam Shea ranked it fifth on his top 10 list of Xbox Live Arcade games. He stated that it was debatable whether an owner of <i>The Orange Box</i> should purchase this, as its added levels do not add to the plot. However, he praised the quality of the new maps included in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The game ranked 7th in a later list of top Xbox Box Live titles compiled by IGN's staff in September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mods">Mods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Mods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Mod_(computer_gaming)" title="Mod (computer gaming)" class="mw-redirect">modding</a> community has developed around <i>Portal</i>, with users creating their own test chambers and other in-game modifications.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The group "We Create Stuff" created an <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a> version of <i>Portal</i>, titled <i>Portal: The Flash Version</i>, just prior to release of <i>The Orange Box</i>. This flash version was well received by the community<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and the group have since converted it to a map pack for the published game.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Another mod, <i>Portal: Prelude</i>, is an unofficial prequel developed by an independent team of three that focuses on the pre-GLaDOS era of Aperture Science, and contains nineteen additional "crafty and challenging" test chambers.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a> version of <i>Portal</i> was created by Joe Larson.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> An unofficial port of <i>Portal</i> to the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> using the <a href="/wiki/Unity_(game_engine)" title="Unity (game engine)">Unity</a> game engine was created but only consisted of a single room from the game.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Mari0" title="Mari0">Mari0</a></i> is a fan-made four-player coop mashup of <i>Portal</i> and the original <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Mario_Bros." title="Super Mario Bros.">Super Mario Bros.</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequel">Sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portal_2" title="Portal 2">Portal 2</a></div>
<p>Swift stated that future <i>Portal</i> developments would depend on the community's reactions, saying, "We're still playing it by ear at this point, figuring out if we want to do multiplayer next, or <i>Portal 2</i>, or release map packs."<sup id="cite_ref-eurogamerfi_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurogamerfi-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Some rumors regarding a sequel arose due to casting calls for voice actors.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> On March 10, 2010, <i>Portal 2</i> was officially announced for a release late in that year;<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> the announcement was preceded by an <a href="/wiki/Alternate_reality_game" title="Alternate reality game">alternate reality game</a> based on unexpected patches made to <i>Portal</i> that contained cryptic messages in relation to <i>Portal 2</i> '​s announcement, including an update to the game, creating a different ending for the fate of Chell. The original game left her in a deserted car park after destroying GLaDOS, but the update involved Chell being dragged back into the facility by a "Party Escort Bot". Though <i>Portal 2</i> was announced for a Q4 2010 release, the game was eventually released on April 19, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-shacknews_update_2_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shacknews_update_2-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Orange_Box#Reception" title="The Orange Box">Critical reception of The Orange Box</a></div>
<table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="collapsible" style="background:transparent;padding:0em;margin:0em 1em 1em 1em;text-align:center;font-size:80%;float:right;clear:right;width:23em">
