<p><i>Portal</i> received critical acclaim, often earning more praise than either <i>Half-Life 2: Episode Two</i> or <i>Team Fortress 2</i>, two titles also included in <i>The Orange Box</i>. It was praised for its unique gameplay and <a href="/wiki/Black_comedy" title="Black comedy">dark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deadpan" title="Deadpan">deadpan</a> humor.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eurogamer" title="Eurogamer">Eurogamer</a> cited that "the way the game progresses from being a simple set of perfunctory tasks to a full-on part of the <i>Half-Life</i> story is absolute genius",<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/GameSpy" title="GameSpy">GameSpy</a> noted that "What <i>Portal</i> lacks in length, it more than makes up for in exhilaration."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The game was criticized for sparse environments, and both criticized and praised for its short length.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Aggregate reviews for the stand-alone PC version of <i>Portal</i> gave the game an average rating of 89% based on 27&#160;reviews through <a href="/wiki/Game_Rankings" title="Game Rankings" class="mw-redirect">Game Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-gamerankings_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamerankings-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> and 90% through 28&#160;reviews on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-metacritic_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon release of <i>Portal 2</i>, Valve stated that <i>Portal</i> has sold more than four million copies through the retail versions, including the standalone game and <i>The Orange Box</i>, and from the Xbox Live Arcade version. This figure does not include sales figures for Valve's own Steam digital download service.<sup id="cite_ref-4million_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4million-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The game generated a fan following for the Weighted Companion Cube<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>—even though the cube itself does not talk or act in the game. Fans have created <a href="/wiki/Stuffed_animal" title="Stuffed animal" class="mw-redirect">plush</a><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Papercraft" title="Papercraft" class="mw-redirect">papercraft</a> versions of the cube and the various turrets,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as PC <a href="/wiki/Case_modding" title="Case modding">case mods</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> and models of the Portal cake and portal gun.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Jeep Barnett, a programmer for <i>Portal</i>, noted that players have told Valve that they had found it more emotional to incinerate the Weighted Companion Cube than to harm one of the "Little Sisters" from <i><a href="/wiki/BioShock" title="BioShock">BioShock</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-1up_beyond_the_box_46-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1up_beyond_the_box-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Both GLaDOS and the Weighted Companion Cube were nominated for the Best New Character Award on G4, with GLaDOS winning the award for "having lines that will be quoted by gamers for years to come."<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ben_Croshaw" title="Ben Croshaw" class="mw-redirect">Ben "Yahtzee" Croshaw</a> of <a href="/wiki/Zero_Punctuation" title="Zero Punctuation">Zero Punctuation</a> gave the game the only entirely positive review in the show's history, calling it "the most fun you'll have with your PC until they invent a force-feedback codpiece". Croshaw went on to say: "I went in expecting a slew of interesting portal-based puzzles and that's exactly what I got, but what I wasn't expecting was some of the funniest pitch black humor I've ever heard in a game". He states that, while the game was short, the two- to three-hour length of the game was perfect as the game did not outstay its welcome, and called the ending "balls-tighteningly fantastic", while praising the game as "absolutely sublime from start to finish".<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Portal</i> '​s story has been stated to be well-established in the context of <a href="/wiki/Erving_Goffman" title="Erving Goffman">Erving Goffman</a>'s dissemination on <a href="/wiki/Dramaturgy_(sociology)" title="Dramaturgy (sociology)">dramaturgy</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Presentation_of_Self_in_Everyday_Life" title="The Presentation of Self in Everyday Life">The Presentation of Self in Everyday Life</a></i>, which equates one's persona to the front and back stage areas of a theater. In the case of <i>Portal</i>, the story carefully establishes the front stage, the pretense of the Enrichment Center, and hints at problems in the back stage through various technical faults, and then slowly reveals more and more of the back stage to the player throughout the game.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to this, the video game was made part of the required course material among other classical and contemporary works, including Goffman's work, for a freshman course "devoted to engaging students with fundamental questions of humanity from multiple perspectives and fostering a sense of community" for <a href="/wiki/Wabash_College" title="Wabash College">Wabash College</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Portal</i> has also been cited as a strong example of <a href="/wiki/Instructional_scaffolding" title="Instructional scaffolding">instructional scaffolding</a> that can be adapted for more academic learning situations, as the player, through careful design of levels by Valve, is first hand-held in solving simple puzzles with many hints at the correct solution, but this support is slowly removed as the player progresses in the game, and completely removed when the player reaches the second half of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rock,_Paper,_Shotgun" title="Rock, Paper, Shotgun">Rock, Paper, Shotgun</a>'s Hamish Todd considered <i>Portal</i> as an exemplary means of game design by demonstrating a series of chambers after the player has obtained the portal gun that gently introduce the concept of flinging without any explicit instructions.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Portal</i> was exhibited at the Smithsonian Art Exhibition in America from February 14 through September 30, 2012. <i>Portal</i> won the "Action" section for the platform "Modern Windows."<sup id="cite_ref-Portal_at_the_Smithsonian_Art_Exhibition_in_America_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portal_at_the_Smithsonian_Art_Exhibition_in_America-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portal_(video_game)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Portal</i> has won several awards:</p>
<ul>
<li>At the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Game_Developers_Choice_Awards" title="Game Developers Choice Awards">Game Developers Choice Awards</a>, <i>Portal</i> won Game of the Year, along with the Innovation Award and Best Game Design.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> honored <i>Portal</i> with several awards, for Best Puzzle Game for PC<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> and Xbox 360,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Most Innovative Design for PC,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> and Best End Credit Song (for "Still Alive") for Xbox 360,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> along with overall honors for Best Puzzle Game<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> and Most Innovative Design.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In its Best of 2007, GameSpot honored <i>The Orange Box</i> with 4 awards in recognition of <i>Portal</i>, giving out honors for Best Puzzle Game,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Best New Character(s) (for GLaDOS),<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> Funniest Game,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> and Best Original Game Mechanic (for the portal gun).<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Portal</i> was awarded Game of the Year (PC), Best Narrative (PC), and Best Innovation (PC and console) honors by 1UP.com in its 2007 editorial awards.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a> honored the game for Most Memorable Villain (for GLaDOS) in its Editors' Choice 2007 Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Portal</i> was awarded the Game of the Year award in 2007 by <a href="/wiki/Joystiq" title="Joystiq">Joystiq</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Good_Game" title="Good Game">Good Game</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Shacknews" title="Shacknews">Shacknews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The Most Original Game award by <i><a href="/wiki/X-Play" title="X-Play">X-Play</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In <i><a href="/wiki/Official_Xbox_Magazine" title="Official Xbox Magazine">Official Xbox Magazine</a></i> '​s 2007 Game of the Year Awards, <i>Portal</i> won Best New Character (for GLaDOS), Best Original Song (for "Still Alive"), and Innovation of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In GameSpy's 2007 Game of the Year awards, <i>Portal</i> was recognized as Best Puzzle Game,<sup id="cite_ref-gamespy-special_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy-special-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Best Character (for GLaDOS), and Best Sidekick (for the Weighted Companion Cube).<sup id="cite_ref-gamespy-special_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gamespy-special-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a> called it the Best Game of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Webcomic" title="Webcomic">webcomic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Penny_Arcade_(webcomic)" title="Penny Arcade (webcomic)" class="mw-redirect">Penny Arcade</a></i> awarded <i>Portal</i> Best Soundtrack, Best Writing, and Best New Game Mechanic in its satirical 2007 We're Right Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eurogamer" title="Eurogamer">Eurogamer</a> gave <i>Portal</i> first place in its Top 50 Games of 2007 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> also placed GLaDOS, (from <i>Portal</i>) as the #1 Video Game Villain on its Top-100 Villains List.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/GamesRadar" title="GamesRadar">GamesRadar</a> named it the best game of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In November 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> named it one of the 100 greatest video games of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-AccoTimeAllTime_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AccoTimeAllTime-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i> considered <i>Portal</i> to be one of the most influential <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_video_gaming" title="2000s in video gaming">games of the first decade of the 21st century</a>, believing it to be the prime example of quality over quantity for video games.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
